<video id='video_player_3742' class='video-js vjs-default-skin' width='480' height='270' controls='controls' preload='auto' poster='/includes/modules/Video_Player/images/video_poster_16x9.jpg'><source src='/assets/cdc/resource/Interview_Documents/After_the_Interview.f4v' type='video/mp4' /><track kind='captions' src='/includes/assets/vtt/?f=/assets/cdc/resource/Interview_Documents/' srclang='en' label='English' default='default' /></video>
<videoadvertising></videoadvertising></component>9. Bumper Cars: Which was worse, Nikki Sorensen being dragged by a photo moto along the road, or the indignity that Johnny Hoogerland and Juan Antonio Flecha experienced during what looked like and attempted mob hit by members of French TV? We have to say the latter and still marvel at the fact that it happened at all. Sure, long breakaways don't always make for great television, but that was a bit over the top.</p></strong><p><strong>8.Winning Yet Not Winning: </strong>One of the big question marks hovering over this year's event was the incredulity surrounding HTC not being able to secure a 2012 sponsor, while simultaneously winning stages at the biggest cycling event in the known galaxy. Rumors now have it that the panic might be over for the uber-successful, but nothing has been confirmed.</p><p><strong>7. To TT Or Not To TT: </strong>That seemed to be the question considering the less than stellar showings at the Grenoble TT by specialists like Fabian Cancellara and Levi Leipheimer. Granted Cancellara had probably already given his all on behalf of the Schlecks, while Levi's motivation had to be somewhat sapped considering his team's run of bad luck. And dark horse fave Robert Gesink apparently didn't learn as much as he told the newspapers that he did when he ran the same course during the Criterium du Dauphine.  </p><p><strong>6.The Fight For White:</strong> The French had more than Thomas Voeckler's epic ride to crow about at this year's Tour. What could be better than having a fellow countryman in yellow? A Frenchman taking a stage victory at the top of Alped'Huez. Heck, his name was even Pierre. And with Pierre Rolland putting in a respectable time trial in Grenoble and receiving final honors in the white jersey competition for best young rider, tongues are already beginning to wag with respect to his chances at a future podium placing. </p><p><strong>5. Spotted Carrot: </strong>Salvaging the pride of the Spanish was none other than Samuel Sanchez, who was one of seven suitors for the King of the Mountains Jerseyduring this year's Tour. The 2008 gold medalist did the business on Luz-Ardiden and took second on the Plateau de Beille. By the time he crossed the finish atop the Alped'Huez he had the polka dot jersey competition sewn up. 5.Sky's The Limit?:Having finally departed Paris with his garment of choice, what can't be said about Mark Cavendish's sprinting prowess at this point that hasn't been said a million times over? This year's Green Jersey winner can still make it look easy as he did on the Champs-Elysees, so perhaps the only lingering question now is how Cav will fare if he indeed does bid the boys who brought him to the line again and again farewell and head to the bluer skies of..er Team Sky for 2012.</p><p><strong>4. Crash Boom Bam!: </strong>Apart from the travesty that was the mob hit on Juan Antonio Flecha and Johnny Hoogerland by the members of French TV, crashes in this year's tour played such a factor that probably should have warranted their own jersey classification. If that were the case Team Radioshack might warrant that award, having lost virtually all of the depth it brought to this year's Tour due to spills. Bradley Wiggins, Dave Zabriskie, and the list goes on. Put it down to nerves, careless spectators or the difficulty of the course, but top shelf bike racing comes with risks, and this year's race proved that out in spades. </p><p><strong>3.Three Strikes.You're Out: </strong>As the @Totalcyclist tweeted out following the conclusion of theTour, the Grenoble TT was only the final "dagger" in Andy Schleck's Tour de France dreams this year. The challenges he continues to face as a descender, and as an inexperienced team leader on the road made up the deadly triad that cost him the victory that was the sole focus of his season. The good news is that he'll be back to try again next year, hopefully more ready to play to his strength and destroy his rivals in the mountains "every" chance he gets.</p><p><strong>2. Voeckler: </strong>If there was ever a more emblematic defense of the maillot jaune drop us a line, because otherwise Thomas Voeckler may own that distinction for quite some time. Every time a seasoned Tour commentator intoned the words "Well, Voeckler will surely surrender the jersey tomorrow." the Cycling Godsresponded by giving the Frenchman just the amount oomph he needed to hang on to yellow. Some say it had to do with an overall cleaner race, but more importantly it had to do with heart of the Europcar rider. If the race had a VIP, he was it. </p><p><strong><component documentid="43872670" type="Video Tease" posted="634471231535500000" updated="634471231535500000" embedded="true" <videoadvertising></videoadvertising></component>Kenny Florian vs. Diego Nunes<br /></strong><br /><strong>Chad Dundas:</strong> Nunes is certainly no patsy for Florian's first foray down to featherweight. With just one career loss in 17 fights, the 28-year-old Brazilian has never been finished and is coming off a split decision win over former champ Mike Brown. That said, so long as Florian isn't sacrificing too much strength and/or stamina to make the weight cut, I think he has the tools to be a force at 145-pounds.<br /><br /><strong>Prediction:</strong>  Florian by unanimous decision<br /><br /><strong>Ariel Helwani:</strong> That's the biggest question going into this one: how will Florian deal with the weight cut? He says he's never felt better, but who expected him to say otherwise? On paper, Florian is more well-rounded, but I think too many people are overlooking the underrated Nunes. Still, I have a hard time picking against Florian in this one, so I won't. I think he will keep the fighting standing en route to a decision win.<br /><br /><strong>Prediction:</strong>  Florian by unanimous decision<br /><br /><br /><strong>John Olav Einemo vs. Dave Herman<br /></strong><br /><strong>Chad Dundas:</strong> Picking a bout between two UFC rookies is always iffy, but there is a lot of anecdotal evidence pointing the way here. Einemo is 35, hasn't fought in MMA since 2006 and was originally brought in as a comeback opponent for Carwin. Meanwhile, Herman is pretty unproven, but still possesses a 20-2 record (one loss via DQ) and the penchant for brutal knockouts the UFC typically looks for in its heavyweights. Figure matchmakers knew what they were doing here. <br /><br /><strong>Prediction:</strong> Herman by second-round TKO.<br /><br /><strong>Ariel Helwani:</strong> Sure, Einemo hasn't fought since 2006, but the Norwegian trains with Golden Glory -- one of the best camps in Europe -- and it's hard to ignore his grappling credentials. So in an effort to gain some ground on ol' Chad, I'm picking Einemo to win this one via submission.<br /><br /><strong>Prediction:</strong> Einemo by second-round submission.<br /><br /><br <video id='video_player_512' class='video-js vjs-default-skin' width='944' height='531' autoplay='autoplay' controls='controls' preload='auto' poster='http://assets.jbu.edu/videos/2013/EVENT_10_05_Homecoming_Highlight/thumb_generated.jpg'><source src='http://assets.jbu.edu/videos/2013/EVENT_10_05_Homecoming_Highlight/video_992x558.mp4' type='video/mp4' /><track kind='captions' src='/includes/assets/vtt/?f=/2013/EVENT_10_05_Homecoming_Highlight/' srclang='en' label='English' default='default' /></video>
<video class="featurette" controls="controls" data-autoplay="true" data-featurette="video-player" data-post-roll-overlay="next-step-overlay" data-record-video-view-url="http://teamtreehouse.com/videos/945/record_video_view" poster="http://wpc.A8B5.edgecastcdn.net/80A8B5/treehouse/stills/THV2-BusinessBay-Island1-Stage5-Video3-FIX-stills-0.jpg?514809d2869d73b56fd93d125510035500c5c9da011d1715abd519c1a2aea0df3e72" preload="none" style="width: 100%; height: 100%"><source src="http://wpc.A8B5.edgecastcdn.net/80A8B5/treehouse/videos/THV2-BusinessBay-Island1-Stage5-Video3-FIX-clip.webm?514809d2869d73b56fd93d125510035500c5c9da011d1715abd519c1a2aea0df3e72" type="video/webm" /><source src="http://wpc.A8B5.edgecastcdn.net/80A8B5/treehouse/videos/THV2-BusinessBay-Island1-Stage5-Video3-FIX-clip.mp4?514809d2869d73b56fd93d125510035500c5c9da011d1715abd519c1a2aea0df3e72" type="video/mp4" /><track kind="subtitles" src="/videos/945/captions" srclang="en" /></video>
<videoadvertising></videoadvertising></component></strong></p><p>The simple thing would be to say no. The simple thing would be to say that all of these 30-something physical specimens who go in for hormone replacement are just using it as a substitute for steroids. They're just looking to cut corners, to get an edge on the competition and the doctors who prescribe them testosterone are shady "anti-aging" types who are either complicit in the scam or willfully ignorant.</p><p>But if Marquardt's appearance on the MMA Hour was a performance or in any way disingenuous, then he is arguably a better actor than he is a fighter. Personally, I found Marquardt and his manager to be pretty credible. In fact, I don't recall a time in any sport where an athlete confronted an allegation of performance enhancers with such candor and seeming honesty. Do I believe him? Yeah, I do. Or at least I want to.</p><p>But I still have doubts. Marquardt certainly fails the "eye test" and - hell - he also already failed one drug test back in 2005. Even if he is telling the truth, I'm not totally convinced his symptoms he described on the show - fatigue, memory loss, irritability - sound quite severe enough to warrant a testosterone exemption for a guy who gets paid to fight other men inside a cage. Then again, I'm not a doctor. I'm also not Nate Marquardt, so I can't claim to know how important to him these treatments are.</p><p>Which brings me to the next question .</p><p><br /><strong>2. Does MMA have a testosterone problem?</strong></p><p>Yes. If it doesn't already, it's about to have one. To my knowledge, Marquart became the fourth high-profile MMA fighter to link himself to TRT today. The other three are Sonnen and - according to a report from Dave Melzter last December - Dan Henderson and Todd Duffee, who both have exemptions to use testosterone in California. To me, that's enough of a trend to warrant some more specific and uniform regulation.</p><p>Obviously, the easiest thing would be for state athletic commissions to decide that no professional athletes really need TRT and to ban it from use during competition. But would there be legal obstacles to that? If guys like Marquardt (or even Sonnen) have legitimate medical conditions that require hormone therapy, I'm not sure you can just effectively bar them from the sport. At least not without a fight in a courtroom somewhere.</p><p>Truth is, if some guys actually do need TRT, then this becomes a far more complicated issue. The athletic commissions are going to have to get together and come up with some standards, or at least make public (and consistent) the standards they already do have. Otherwise, this could be an issue that the sport is dealing with for a long time.</p><p><br /><strong>3. <video id='video_player_7149' class='video-js vjs-default-skin' width='944' height='531' autoplay='autoplay' controls='controls' preload='auto' poster='http://assets.jbu.edu/videos/2011/EVENT_20110315_Arsenic_and_Old_Lace/thumb_generated.jpg'><source src='http://assets.jbu.edu/videos/2011/EVENT_20110315_Arsenic_and_Old_Lace/video_992x558.mp4' type='video/mp4' /><track kind='captions' src='/includes/assets/vtt/?f=/2011/EVENT_20110315_Arsenic_and_Old_Lace/' srclang='en' label='English' default='default' /></video>
<videoadvertising></videoadvertising></component>NL Cy Young</strong>: The statistical difference between favorite Clayton Kershaw and still-unknown Atlanta pitcher Brandon Beachy boils down to Kershaw's better strikeout-walk ratio (4-1 to 3-1). Which makes Beachy's story all the better: Undrafted free agent out of Indiana Wesleyan University, signed for $20,000, started his minor-league career in the bullpen, and four years later, a Cy Young-caliber starter. </p><p><strong>AL Manager of the Year</strong>: It can only be Buck Showalter, as the Orioles were a near-unanimous spring choice for another last-place finish in the AL East. Nobody knows how long they can hang around, but there are enough positive signs throughout the organization for legitimate optimism. This also could be the year Manny Acta gets his due, while Joe Maddon remains the most interesting manager in the world. </p><p><strong>NL Manager of the Year</strong>: Nobody was paying attention when the Dodgers turned the corner last August and went 34-20 down the stretch. But everybody is aware of Don Mattingly's team now, as it sat 30 games over .500 at 64-34 in its last 98 games through Wednesday. </p><p>It's who Mattingly is winning with that makes his case. Kemp, Mark Ellis, Juan Rivera, Juan Uribe, Jerry Hairston Jr. currently are on the disabled list, Dee Gordon was benched then dropped to eighth in the order, and James Loney's power struggles continue. Yet the wins keep mounting with lineups including Jerry Sands, Justin Sellers, Elian Herrara, Scott Van Slyke and Ivan DeJesus. </p><p><strong>AL Rookie of the Year</strong>: He's no rookie, of course -- not when it took over $100 million to get him out of Japan. But Yu Darvish is eligible for the award and gets it at this point. But Mike Trout is making it interesting, isn't he? </p><p><strong>NL Rookie of the Year</strong>: We know where this likely is leading as the season unfolds -- Bryce Harper. Especially when this isn't a particularly strong year for NL rookies. Wade Miley, Yonder Alonso, Zack Cozart and Kirk Nieuwenhuis are off to nice starts. </p><p><strong><component documentid="47543513" type="Video Tease" posted="634734152555330000" updated="634734152705570000" embedded="true" site="21683474"><align>right</align><iconsetting><hidetimestampicon>false</hidetimestampicon><hidecontenticon>false</hidecontenticon></iconsetting><tease><filename>s_nbc_mlb_sportstalkretaliation_120523</filename><layout id="3"><value>3</value><enumitem id="3" value="Main Art (275)"></enumitem></layout><image><component documentid="47543504" type="Image" site="21683474" updated="634734131341570000" changed="634734131351200000"><layout><filename>/NBCSports/Components/Video/_NEW/s_nbc_mlb_sportstalkretaliation_120523_4x3.jpg</filename><size id="1"><value>1</value><enumitem id="1" value="Standard"></enumitem></size><width>640</width><height>480</height><verticalmargin>0</verticalmargin><horizontalmargin>0</horizontalmargin><noresize>false</noresize><bordercolor>#000000</bordercolor><mediaroot2><a href="http://msnbcmedia.msn.com">http://msnbcmedia.msn.com</a></mediaroot2></layout><credits><byline>Rich Lipski</byline><source>FR170623 AP</source><credits>AP</credits></credits><caption><caption>Washington Nationals' batter Bryce Harper is hit by the pitch thrown by Philadelphia Phillies pitcher Cole Hamels during the first inning of their baseball game at Nationals Park, Sunday, May 6, 2012, in Washington. Robert Meachem and Marques Colston, Saints</strong>: The soon-to-be free agent wideouts for the Saints can make some money with a big playoff run.</p><p><strong>5. Ryan Grant, Packers</strong>: He represents all the injured Packers from a year ago that only could watch their team win it all. Grant has possibly played his way into another year in Green Bay with a strong finish to the season. </p><p><strong>6. Tim Tebow, Broncos</strong>: The guy needs more attention. </p><p><strong>PLAYERS WITH MOST TO LOSE<br />1. Tom Brady, Patriots</strong>: This game means so much to the Patriots. A third straight playoff defeat at home would be devastating for Brady. He seems more driven then ever at age 34, almost like he wants another title <em>too </em>much.  He knows the Patriots can't be No. 1 seeds forever.</p><p><strong>2. Ray Lewis, Ravens</strong>: He says this team is more complete than the 2000 Ravens. Terrell Suggs says this is easily the best Ravens team he's played on. <videoadvertising></videoadvertising></component>3. Joe Flacco, Ravens</strong>: If he thought the media didn't give him credit before, try losing to a fifth-round rookie quarterback at home. </p><p><strong>4. Charles Woodson, Packers</strong>: Woodson said it during the week. Two straight titles would put the Packers at a different level historically. This team seems very aware of how close it is to being an all-time great. </p><p><strong>5. Sean Payton, Saints</strong>: It's not particularly fair, but the Saints' winning streak has left many in New Orleans feeling that anything short of a Super Bowl title this year will be a massive disappointment. </p><p><strong>MATCHUPS TO WATCH<br /></strong><strong>1. Jason Pierre-Paul versus Chad Clifton<br /></strong>Green Bay did a decent job protecting Aaron Rodgers in the first matchup against the Giants with one huge exception. Jason Pierre-Paul absolutely manhandled left tackle Marshall Newhouse all day. </p><p>Now Chad Clifton is back after taking only 25 snaps in Week 17. He hasn't played a full game since Week 4. It's a tall task to ask Clifton to hold up against JPP on the outside. Packers right tackle Bryan Bulaga is also coming back from an injury and will be tested by New York's pass rush. </p><p><strong>2. Patriots tight ends versus Broncos safeties<br /></strong>Denver double-teamed Rob Gronkowski all day last time around, so Aaron Hernandez went off for nine catches and 129 yards. New England exposed the youth at safety and the lack of depth in Denver's secondary last time. I doubt they found a solution in the meantime.</p><p><strong><component documentid="45979320" type="Video Tease" posted="634620134241270000" updated="634620134577130000" embedded="true" site="21683474"><align>right</align><iconsetting><hidetimestampicon>false</hidetimestampicon><hidecontenticon>false</hidecontenticon></iconsetting><tease><filename>s_nbc_nfl_sportstalkhoubal_120112</filename><layout id="2"><value>2</value><enumitem id="2" value="Horizontal (300)"></enumitem></layout><image><component documentid="45979224" type="Image" site="21683474" updated="634620116939430000" changed="634620116952700000"><layout><filename>/NBCSports/Components/Video/_NEW/s_nbc_nfl_sportstalkhoubal_120112_4x3.jpg</filename><size id="1"><value>1</value><enumitem id="1" value="Standard"></enumitem></size><width>640</width><height>480</height><verticalmargin>0</verticalmargin><horizontalmargin>0</horizontalmargin><noresize>false</noresize><bordercolor>#000000</bordercolor><mediaroot2><a href="http://msnbcmedia.msn.com">http://msnbcmedia.msn.com</a></mediaroot2></layout><credits><byline>Rob Carr</byline><source>Getty Images North America</source><credits>Getty Images</credits><copyright>2011 Getty Images</copyright></credits><caption><caption>BALTIMORE, MD - OCTOBER 16: Running back  Ray Rice #27 of the Baltimore Ravens carries the ball while defender Tim Jamison #96 of the Houston Texans looks on during the second half at M&amp;T Bank Stadium on October 16, 2011 in Baltimore, Maryland.
